e=()=>{document.removeEventListener("DOMContentLoaded",e),c.disconnect(),this.childrenConnectedCallback()},c=new MutationObserver(()=>{var n;((n=this.lastChild)==null?void 0:n.nodeType)===Node.COMMENT_NODE&&this.lastChild.nodeValue==="astro:end"&&(this.lastChild.remove(),e())});c.observe(this,{childList:!0}),document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded",e)}}async childrenConnectedCallback(){let e=this.getAttribute("before-hydration-url");e&&await import(e),this.start()}async start(){let e=JSON.parse(this.getAttribute("opts")),c=this.getAttribute("client");if(Astro[c]===void 0){window.addEventListener(`astro:${c}`,()=>this.start(),{once:!0});return}try{await Astro[c](async()=>{let uid="Z1ViS7v" prefix="r7" component-url="/_astro/PostCopyButton.-PGtk4At.js" component-export="default" renderer-url="/_astro/client.DGA1VMK9.js" props="{&quot;title&quot;:[0,&quot;How to build Microfrontends with Module Federation and Vue&quot;],&quot;content&quot;:[0,&quot;import Alert from \&quot;@features/mdx-components/components/Alert.astro\&quot;;\nimport Figure from \&quot;@features/mdx-components/components/Figure.astro\&quot;;\nimport YouTube from \&quot;@features/mdx-components/components/YouTube.astro\&quot;;\nimport MicrofrontendPubSub from \&quot;@features/local-first/components/MicrofrontendPubSub.tsx\&quot;;\nimport tractorStoreImage from \&quot;../../assets/images/vueMicro/tractorStoreVue.png\&quot;;\n\n&lt;Alert type=\&quot;tip\&quot; title=\&quot;TL;DR\&quot;&gt;\n  Monorepo with `pnpm`. Vue 3 SPA. Client side composition with Module\n  Federation. Host owns routing. Events for navigation. Cart sync through\n  localStorage plus events. Shared UI library for consistency. Fallbacks for\n  remote failures. Code:\n  https://github.com/alexanderop/tractorStoreVueModuleFederation\n&lt;/Alert&gt;\n\n&lt;Alert type=\&quot;warning\&quot; title=\&quot;Who should read this\&quot;&gt;\n  You know Vue and basic bundling. You want to split a SPA into independent\n  parts without tight coupling. If you do not have multiple teams or deployment\n  bottlenecks, you likely do not need microfrontends.\n&lt;/Alert&gt;\n\nI wanted to write about microfrontends three years ago. My first touchpoint was the book _Micro Frontends in Action_ by Michael Geers. It taught me a lot, and I was still confused. This post shows a practical setup that works today with Vue 3 and Module Federation.\n\n## Scope\n\nWe build microfrontends for a Vue 3 SPA with client side composition. Server and universal rendering exist, but they are out of scope here.\n\n&gt; Microfrontends are the technical representation of a business subdomain. They allow independent implementations with minimal shared code and single team ownership.\n&gt; (Luca Mezzalira)\n\n## The Tractor Store in one minute\n\nThe Tractor Store is a reference shop that lets us compare microfrontend approaches on the same feature set (explore, decide, checkout). It is clear enough to show boundaries and realistic enough to surface routing, shared state, and styling issues.\n\n&lt;YouTube\n  id=\&quot;12TN7Zq7VxM\&quot;\n  title=\&quot;The Tractor Store idea\&quot;\n  caption=\&quot;If you want to understand the background and the full setup behind the Tractor Store exercise, watch the video of the creator: https://micro-frontends.org/tractor-store/\&quot;\n/&gt;\n\n&lt;Figure\n  src={tractorStoreImage}\n  alt=\&quot;Tractor Store application overview showing the microfrontend architecture with product listings, recommendations, and shopping cart functionality\&quot;\n  width={800}\n  caption=\&quot;The Tractor Store built with Vue 3 microfrontends and Module Federation\&quot;\n/&gt;\n\n## Architecture decisions\n\n| Question         | Decision                                                        | Notes                                              |\n| ---------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------- |\n| Repo layout      | Monorepo with `pnpm` workspaces                                 | Shared configs, atomic refactors, simple local dev |\n| Composition      | Client side with Module Federation                              | Fast iteration, simple hosting                     |\n| Routing          | Host owns routing                                               | One place for guards, links, and errors            |\n| Team boundaries  | Explore, Decide, Checkout, plus Host                            | Map to clear user flows                            |\n| Communication    | Custom events for navigation. Cart via localStorage plus events | Low coupling and no shared global store            |\n| UI consistency   | Shared UI library in `packages/shared`                          | Buttons, inputs, tokens                            |\n| Failure handling | Loading and error fallbacks in host. Retry once                 | Keep the shell usable                              |\n| Styles           | Team prefixes or Vue scoped styles. Tokens in shared            | Prevent leakage and keep a common look             |\n\nRepository layout:\n\n```\n├── apps/\n│   ├── host/          (Shell application)\n│   ├── explore/       (Product discovery)\n│   ├── decide/        (Product detail)\n│   └── checkout/      (Cart and checkout)\n├── packages/\n│   └── shared/        (UI, tokens, utils)\n└── pnpm-workspace.yaml\n```\n\nWorkspace definition:\n\n```yaml\npackages:\n  - \&quot;apps/*\&quot;\n  - \&quot;packages/*\&quot;\n```\n\nHigh level view:\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    subgraph \&quot;Monorepo (@tractor)\&quot;\n        subgraph \&quot;apps/\&quot;\n            Host(\&quot;host\&quot;)\n            Explore(\&quot;explore\&quot;)\n            Decide(\&quot;decide\&quot;)\n            Checkout(\&quot;checkout\&quot;)\n        end\n        subgraph \&quot;packages/\&quot;\n            Shared(\&quot;shared\&quot;)\n        end\n    end\n\n    Host -- Consumes --&gt; Explore\n    Host -- Consumes --&gt; Decide\n    Host -- Consumes --&gt; Checkout\n\n    Explore -- Uses --&gt; Shared\n    Decide -- Uses --&gt; Shared\n    Checkout -- Uses --&gt; Shared\n    Host -- Uses --&gt; Shared\n```\n\n## Implementation\n\nWe compose at the client in the host. The host loads remote components at runtime and routes between them.\n\n### Host router\n\n```ts\n// apps/host/src/router.ts\nimport { createRouter, createWebHistory } from \&quot;vue-router\&quot;;\nimport { remote } from \&quot;../utils/remote\&quot;;\n\nexport const router = createRouter({\n  history: createWebHistory(),\n  routes: [\n    { path: \&quot;/\&quot;, component: remote(\&quot;explore/HomePage\&quot;) },\n    {\n      path: \&quot;/products/:category?\&quot;,\n      component: remote(\&quot;explore/CategoryPage\&quot;),\n      props: true,\n    },\n    {\n      path: \&quot;/product/:id\&quot;,\n      component: remote(\&quot;decide/ProductPage\&quot;),\n      props: true,\n    },\n    { path: \&quot;/checkout/cart\&quot;, component: remote(\&quot;checkout/CartPage\&quot;) },\n  ],\n});\n```\n\n### `remote()` utility\n\n&lt;Alert type=\&quot;tip\&quot; title=\&quot;Vue async components\&quot;&gt;\nVue `defineAsyncComponent` wraps any loader in a friendly component. It gives lazy loading, built in states, and retries. This is why it fits microfrontends.\n\n```js\nimport { defineAsyncComponent } from \&quot;vue\&quot;;\n\nconst AsyncComp = defineAsyncComponent({\n  loader: () =&gt; Promise.resolve(/* component */),\n  delay: 200,\n  timeout: 3000,\n  onError(error, retry, fail, attempts) {\n    if (attempts &lt;= 1) retry();\n    else fail();\n  },\n});\n```\n\n&lt;/Alert&gt;\n\n```ts\n// apps/host/src/utils/remote.ts\nimport { defineAsyncComponent, h } from \&quot;vue\&quot;;\n\nexport function remote(id: string, delay = 150) {\n  return defineAsyncComponent({\n    loader: async () =&gt; {\n      const loader = (window as any).getComponent?.(id);\n      if (!loader) throw new Error(`Missing loader for ${id}`);\n      return await loader();\n    },\n    delay,\n    loadingComponent: {\n      render: () =&gt; h(\&quot;div\&quot;, { class: \&quot;mf-loading\&quot; }, \&quot;Loading...\&quot;),\n    },\n    errorComponent: {\n      render: () =&gt; h(\&quot;div\&quot;, { class: \&quot;mf-error\&quot; }, \&quot;Failed to load.\&quot;),\n    },\n    onError(error, retry, fail, attempts) {\n      if (attempts &lt;= 1) setTimeout(retry, 200);\n      else fail();\n    },\n  });\n}\n```\n\n&lt;Alert type=\&quot;note\&quot; title=\&quot;💡 What is Module Federation?\&quot;&gt;\n  Module Federation enables dynamic loading of JavaScript modules from different\n  applications at runtime. Think of it as splitting your app into independently\n  deployable pieces that can share code and communicate. You can use **Webpack\n  5**, **Rspack**, or **Vite** as bundlers. **Rspack offers the most\n  comprehensive Module Federation support** with excellent performance, but for\n  this solution I used **Rspack** (for the host) and **Vite** (for one remote)\n  to showcase interoperability between different bundlers.\n&lt;/Alert&gt;\n\n### Module Federation runtime\n\nThe host bootstraps Module Federation and exposes a single loader.\n\n```ts\n// apps/host/src/mf.ts\nimport {\n  createInstance,\n  loadRemote,\n} from \&quot;@module-federation/enhanced/runtime\&quot;;\n\ndeclare global {\n  interface Window {\n    getComponent: (id: string) =&gt; () =&gt; Promise&lt;any&gt;;\n  }\n}\n\ncreateInstance({\n  name: \&quot;host\&quot;,\n  remotes: [\n    {\n      name: \&quot;decide\&quot;,\n      entry: \&quot;http://localhost:5175/mf-manifest.json\&quot;,\n      alias: \&quot;decide\&quot;,\n    },\n    {\n      name: \&quot;explore\&quot;,\n      entry: \&quot;http://localhost:3004/mf-manifest.json\&quot;,\n      alias: \&quot;explore\&quot;,\n    },\n    {\n      name: \&quot;checkout\&quot;,\n      entry: \&quot;http://localhost:3003/mf-manifest.json\&quot;,\n      alias: \&quot;checkout\&quot;,\n    },\n  ],\n  plugins: [\n    {\n      name: \&quot;fallback-plugin\&quot;,\n      errorLoadRemote(args: any) {\n        console.warn(`Failed to load remote: ${args.id}`, args.error);\n        return {\n          default: {\n            template: `&lt;div style=\&quot;padding: 2rem; text-align: center; border: 1px solid #ddd; border-radius: 8px; background: #f9f9f9; margin: 1rem 0;\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;h3 style=\&quot;color: #c00; margin-bottom: 1rem;\&quot;&gt;Remote unavailable&lt;/h3&gt;\n              &lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Remote:&lt;/strong&gt; ${args.id}&lt;/p&gt;\n              &lt;p&gt;Try again or check the service.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;/div&gt;`,\n          },\n        };\n      },\n    },\n  ],\n});\n\nwindow.getComponent = (id: string) =&gt; {\n  return async () =&gt; {\n    const mod = (await loadRemote(id)) as any;\n    return mod.default || mod;\n  };\n};\n```\n\n**Why this setup**\n\n- The host is the single source of truth for remote URLs and versions.\n- URLs can change without rebuilding remotes.\n- The fallback plugin gives a consistent error experience.\n\n## Communication\n\nWe avoid a shared global store. We use two small patterns that keep coupling low.\n\n&lt;Alert type=\&quot;important\&quot; title=\&quot;Why we do not need Pinia\&quot;&gt;\nA global store looks handy. In microfrontends it creates tight runtime coupling. That kills independent deploys.\n\nWhat goes wrong:\n\n- Lockstep releases (one store change breaks other teams)\n- Hidden contracts (store shape is an API that drifts)\n- Boot order traps (who creates the store and plugins)\n- Bigger blast radius (a store error can break the whole app)\n- Harder tests (cross team mocks and brittle fixtures)\n\nDo this instead:\n\n- Each microfrontend owns its state\n- Communicate with explicit custom events\n- Use URL and localStorage for simple shared reads\n- Share code not state (tokens, UI, pure utils)\n- If shared state grows, revisit boundaries rather than centralize it\n&lt;/Alert&gt;\n\n&lt;Alert type=\&quot;info\&quot; title=\&quot;💡 Alternative: VueUse EventBus\&quot;&gt;\n  You could use VueUse&#39;s `useEventBus` for more Vue-like event communication\n  instead of vanilla JavaScript events. It provides a cleaner API with\n  TypeScript support and automatic cleanup in component lifecycle. However,\n  adding VueUse means another dependency in your microfrontends. The tradeoff is\n  developer experience vs. bundle size and dependency management: vanilla\n  JavaScript events keep things lightweight and framework-agnostic.\n&lt;/Alert&gt;\n\n### Navigation through custom events\n\nRemotes dispatch `mf:navigate` with `{ to }`. The host listens and calls `router.push`.\n\n```ts\n// apps/host/src/main.ts\nwindow.addEventListener(\&quot;mf:navigate\&quot;, (e: Event) =&gt; {\n  const to = (e as CustomEvent).detail?.to;\n  if (to) router.push(to);\n});\n```\n\n### Cart sync through localStorage plus events\n\nThe checkout microfrontend owns cart logic. It listens for `add-to-cart` and `remove-from-cart`. After each change, it writes to localStorage and dispatches `updated-cart`. Any component can listen and re read.\n\n```ts\n// apps/checkout/src/stores/cartStore.ts\nwindow.addEventListener(\&quot;add-to-cart\&quot;, (ev: Event) =&gt; {\n  const { sku } = (ev as CustomEvent).detail;\n  // update cart array here\n  localStorage.setItem(\&quot;cart\&quot;, JSON.stringify(cart));\n  window.dispatchEvent(new CustomEvent(\&quot;updated-cart\&quot;));\n});\n```\n\n&lt;MicrofrontendPubSub client:load /&gt;\n\n## Styling\n\n- Design tokens in `packages/shared` (CSS variables).\n- Shared UI in `packages/shared/ui` (Button, Input, Card).\n- Local isolation with Vue scoped styles or BEM with team prefixes (`e_`, `d_`, `c_`, `h_`).\n- Host provides `.mf-loading` and `.mf-error` classes for fallback UI.\n\nExample with BEM plus team prefix:\n\n```css\n/* decide */\n.d_ProductPage__title {\n  font-size: 2rem;\n  color: var(--color-primary);\n}\n.d_ProductPage__title--featured {\n  color: var(--color-accent);\n}\n```\n\nOr Vue scoped styles:\n\n```vue\n&lt;template&gt;\n  &lt;div class=\&quot;product-information\&quot;&gt;\n    &lt;h1 class=\&quot;title\&quot;&gt;{{ product.name }}&lt;/h1&gt;\n  &lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;/template&gt;\n\n&lt;style scoped&gt;\n.product-information {\n  padding: 1rem;\n}\n.title {\n  font-size: 2rem;\n}\n&lt;/style&gt;\n```\n\n## Operations\n\nPlan for failure and keep the shell alive.\n\n- Each remote shows a clear loading state and a clear error state.\n- Navigation works even if a remote fails.\n- Logs are visible in the host during development.\n\nGlobal styles in the host help here:\n\n```css\n/* apps/host/src/styles.css */\n.mf-loading {\n  display: flex;\n  align-items: center;\n  justify-content: center;\n  padding: 2rem;\n  color: var(--color-text-muted);\n}\n\n.mf-error {\n  padding: 1rem;\n  background: var(--color-error-background);\n  border: 1px solid var(--color-error-border);\n  color: var(--color-error-text);\n  border-radius: 4px;\n}\n```\n\n## More Module Federation features (short hints)\n\nOur solution is simple on purpose. Module Federation can do more. Use these when your app needs them.\n\n**Prefetch** (requires registering lazyLoadComponentPlugin)  \nPre load JS, CSS, and data for a remote before the user clicks (for example on hover). This cuts wait time.\n\n```js\n// after registering lazyLoadComponentPlugin on the runtime instance\nimport { getInstance } from \&quot;@module-federation/enhanced/runtime\&quot;;\n\nconst mf = getInstance();\nfunction onHover() {\n  mf.prefetch({\n    id: \&quot;shop/Button\&quot;,\n    dataFetchParams: { productId: \&quot;12345\&quot; },\n    preloadComponentResource: true, // also fetch JS and CSS\n  });\n}\n```\n\n**Component level data fetching**  \nExpose a `.data` loader next to a component. The consumer can ask the runtime to fetch data before render (works in CSR and SSR). Use a `.data.client.ts` file for client loaders when SSR falls back.\n\n**Caching for loaders**  \nWrap expensive loaders in a cache helper (with maxAge, revalidate, tag, and custom keys). You get stale while revalidate behavior and tag based invalidation.\n\n```js\n// inside your DataLoader file\nconst fetchDashboard = cache(async () =&gt; getStats(), {\n  maxAge: 120000,\n  revalidate: 60000,\n});\n```\n\n**Type hinting for remotes**  \n`@module-federation/enhanced` can generate types for exposes. Add this to tsconfig.json so editors resolve remote types and hot reload them.\n\n```json\n{\n  \&quot;compilerOptions\&quot;: { \&quot;paths\&quot;: { \&quot;*\&quot;: [\&quot;./@mf-types/*\&quot;] } },\n  \&quot;include\&quot;: [\&quot;./@mf-types/*\&quot;]\n}\n```\n\n**Vue bridge for app level modules**  \nMount a whole remote Vue app into a route when you need an application level integration (not just a component).\n\n```js\nimport { createRemoteAppComponent } from \&quot;@module-federation/bridge-vue3\&quot;;\nconst RemoteApp = createRemoteAppComponent({\n  loader: () =&gt; loadRemote(\&quot;remote1/export-app\&quot;),\n});\n// router: { path: &#39;/remote1/:pathMatch(.*)*&#39;, component: RemoteApp }\n```\n\nYou can read more about these interesting techniques at [module-federation.io](https://module-federation.io/).\n\n### Summary\n\nThis was my first attempt to understand **microfrontends** better while solving the _Tractor Store_ exercise.\n\nIn the future, I may also try it with **SSR** and **universal rendering**, which I find interesting.\n\nAnother option could be to use **Nuxt Layers** and take a _“microfrontend-ish”_ approach at build time.&quot;]}" ssr client="load" opts="{&quot;name&quot;:&quot;PostCopyButton&quot;,&quot;value&quot;:true}" await-children><button class="focus-outline inline-flex items-center gap-1.5 rounded-md border border-skin-line bg-skin-card px-2.5 py-1.5 text-xs font-medium text-skin-base opacity-80 transition-all hover:border-skin-accent/50 hover:text-skin-accent hover:opacity-100" aria-label="Copy post as markdown" title="Copy post as markdown for AI/LLM"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" class="h-3.5 w-3.5" viewBox="0 0 20 20" fill="currentColor"><path d="M8 3a1 1 0 011-1h2a1 1 0 110 2H9a1 1 0 01-1-1z"></path><path d="M6 3a2 2 0 00-2 2v11a2 2 0 002 2h8a2 2 0 002-2V5a2 2 0 00-2-2 3 3 0 01-3 3H9a3 3 0 01-3-3z"></path></svg><span>Copy Post</span></button><!--astro:end--></astro-island> </div> <nav class="mb-8 astro-sbmhws2g" aria-labelledby="series-heading"> <div class="mb-1 text-sm font-bold tracking-wide text-skin-accent astro-sbmhws2g"> Vue Architecture Guide </div> <h2 id="series-heading" class="mb-2 text-xs font-semibold uppercase tracking-widest text-skin-accent astro-sbmhws2g">

Vue 3 SPA. Client side composition with Module
Federation. Host owns routing. Events for navigation. Cart sync through
localStorage plus events. Shared UI library for consistency. Fallbacks for
remote failures. Code:
<a href="https://github.com/alexanderop/tractorStoreVueModuleFederation" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">https://github.com/alexanderop/tractorStoreVueModuleFederation</a></p> </div> </div> 
<div class="alert alert-warning astro-7kdbuayl"> <p class="alert-title astro-7kdbuayl"> <span class="alert-icon astro-7kdbuayl">⚠️</span> Who should read this </p> <div class="alert-content astro-7kdbuayl"> <p>You know Vue and basic bundling. You want to split a SPA into independent
parts without tight coupling. If you do not have multiple teams or deployment
bottlenecks, you likely do not need microfrontends.</p> </div> </div> 
<p>I wanted to write about microfrontends three years ago. My first touchpoint was the book <em>Micro Frontends in Action</em> by Michael Geers. It taught me a lot, and I was still confused. This post shows a practical setup that works today with Vue 3 and Module Federation.</p>
<h2 id="scope">Scope<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#scope"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<p>We build microfrontends for a Vue 3 SPA with client side composition. Server and universal rendering exist, but they are out of scope here.</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Microfrontends are the technical representation of a business subdomain. They allow independent implementations with minimal shared code and single team ownership.
(Luca Mezzalira)</p>
</blockquote>
<h2 id="the-tractor-store-in-one-minute">The Tractor Store in one minute<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#the-tractor-store-in-one-minute"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<p>The Tractor Store is a reference shop that lets us compare microfrontend approaches on the same feature set (explore, decide, checkout). It is clear enough to show boundaries and realistic enough to surface routing, shared state, and styling issues.</p>
<div class="mb-8"> <div class="relative w-full pb-[56.25%]"> <iframe src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/12TN7Zq7VxM" title="The Tractor Store idea" class="absolute left-0 top-0 h-full w-full rounded-lg" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen></iframe> </div> <p class="mt-3 text-center text-sm italic text-gray-500">If you want to understand the background and the full setup behind the Tractor Store exercise, watch the video of the creator: https://micro-frontends.org/tractor-store/</p> </div>
<figure class=" mx-auto "> <img src="/_astro/tractorStoreVue.Lx0ePLIa_Z1bDjpo.webp" alt="Tractor Store application overview showing the microfrontend architecture with product listings, recommendations, and shopping cart functionality" loading="lazy" decoding="async" fetchpriority="auto" width="800" height="425" class="w-full"> <figcaption class="mt-2 text-center text-sm text-gray-500"> The Tractor Store built with Vue 3 microfrontends and Module Federation </figcaption> </figure>
<h2 id="architecture-decisions">Architecture decisions<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#architecture-decisions"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>


















































<table><thead><tr><th>Question</th><th>Decision</th><th>Notes</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td data-label="Question">Repo layout</td><td data-label="Decision">Monorepo with <code>pnpm</code> workspaces</td><td data-label="Notes">Shared configs, atomic refactors, simple local dev</td></tr><tr><td data-label="Question">Composition</td><td data-label="Decision">Client side with Module Federation</td><td data-label="Notes">Fast iteration, simple hosting</td></tr><tr><td data-label="Question">Routing</td><td data-label="Decision">Host owns routing</td><td data-label="Notes">One place for guards, links, and errors</td></tr><tr><td data-label="Question">Team boundaries</td><td data-label="Decision">Explore, Decide, Checkout, plus Host</td><td data-label="Notes">Map to clear user flows</td></tr><tr><td data-label="Question">Communication</td><td data-label="Decision">Custom events for navigation. Cart via localStorage plus events</td><td data-label="Notes">Low coupling and no shared global store</td></tr><tr><td data-label="Question">UI consistency</td><td data-label="Decision">Shared UI library in <code>packages/shared</code></td><td data-label="Notes">Buttons, inputs, tokens</td></tr><tr><td data-label="Question">Failure handling</td><td data-label="Decision">Loading and error fallbacks in host. Retry once</td><td data-label="Notes">Keep the shell usable</td></tr><tr><td data-label="Question">Styles</td><td data-label="Decision">Team prefixes or Vue scoped styles. Tokens in shared</td><td data-label="Notes">Prevent leakage and keep a common look</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Repository layout:</p>
<pre class="astro-code tokyo-night" style="background-color:#1a1b26;color:#a9b1d6;overflow-x:auto;white-space:pre-wrap;word-wrap:break-word" tabindex="0" data-language="plaintext"><code><span class="line"><span>├── apps/</span></span>
<span class="line"><span>│   ├── host/          (Shell application)</span></span>
<span class="line"><span>│   ├── explore/       (Product discovery)</span></span>
<span class="line"><span>│   ├── decide/        (Product detail)</span></span>
<span class="line"><span>│   └── checkout/      (Cart and checkout)</span></span>
<span class="line"><span>├── packages/</span></span>
<span class="line"><span>│   └── shared/        (UI, tokens, utils)</span></span>
<span class="line"><span>└── pnpm-workspace.yaml</span></span></code><button type="button" class="copy" data-code="├── apps/
│   ├── host/          (Shell application)

│   ├── decide/        (Product detail)
│   └── checkout/      (Cart and checkout)
├── packages/
│   └── shared/        (UI, tokens, utils)
└── pnpm-workspace.yaml" onclick="

<h2 id="implementation">Implementation<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#implementation"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<p>We compose at the client in the host. The host loads remote components at runtime and routes between them.</p>
<h3 id="host-router">Host router<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#host-router"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>

import { remote } from &#34;../utils/remote&#34;;

export const router = createRouter({
  history: createWebHistory(),
  routes: [
    { path: &#34;/&#34;, component: remote(&#34;explore/HomePage&#34;) },
    {
      path: &#34;/products/:category?&#34;,

      path: &#34;/product/:id&#34;,

<h3 id="remote-utility"><code>remote()</code> utility<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#remote-utility"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<div class="alert alert-tip astro-7kdbuayl"> <p class="alert-title astro-7kdbuayl"> <span class="alert-icon astro-7kdbuayl">💪</span> Vue async components </p> <div class="alert-content astro-7kdbuayl"> <p>Vue <code>defineAsyncComponent</code> wraps any loader in a friendly component. It gives lazy loading, built in states, and retries. This is why it fits microfrontends.</p><pre class="astro-code tokyo-night" style="background-color:#1a1b26;color:#a9b1d6;overflow-x:auto;white-space:pre-wrap;word-wrap:break-word" tabindex="0" data-language="js"><code><span class="line"><span style="color:#7DCFFF">import</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> { </span><span style="color:#0DB9D7">defineAsyncComponent</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> }</span><span style="color:#7DCFFF"> from</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> &quot;</span><span style="color:#9ECE6A">vue</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>

<span class="line"><span style="color:#9ABDF5">}</span></span></code><button type="button" class="copy" data-code="// apps/host/src/utils/remote.ts
import { defineAsyncComponent, h } from &#34;vue&#34;;

export function remote(id: string, delay = 150) {
  return defineAsyncComponent({
    loader: async () => {
      const loader = (window as any).getComponent?.(id);
      if (!loader) throw new Error(`Missing loader for ${id}`);
      return await loader();
    },
    delay,
    loadingComponent: {
      render: () => h(&#34;div&#34;, { class: &#34;mf-loading&#34; }, &#34;Loading...&#34;),
    },
    errorComponent: {
      render: () => h(&#34;div&#34;, { class: &#34;mf-error&#34; }, &#34;Failed to load.&#34;),
    },
    onError(error, retry, fail, attempts) {
      if (attempts <= 1) setTimeout(retry, 200);
      else fail();
    },
  });
}" onclick="
            navigator.clipboard.writeText(this.dataset.code);
            this.classList.add('copied');
            setTimeout(() => this.classList.remove('copied'), 3000);
          " aria-label="Copy code"><span class="ready"></span><span class="success"></span></button></pre>
<div class="alert alert-note astro-7kdbuayl"> <p class="alert-title astro-7kdbuayl"> <span class="alert-icon astro-7kdbuayl">💡</span> 💡 What is Module Federation? </p> <div class="alert-content astro-7kdbuayl"> <p>Module Federation enables dynamic loading of JavaScript modules from different
applications at runtime. Think of it as splitting your app into independently
deployable pieces that can share code and communicate. You can use <strong>Webpack
5</strong>, <strong>Rspack</strong>, or <strong>Vite</strong> as bundlers. <strong>Rspack offers the most
comprehensive Module Federation support</strong> with excellent performance, but for
this solution I used <strong>Rspack</strong> (for the host) and <strong>Vite</strong> (for one remote)
to showcase interoperability between different bundlers.</p> </div> </div> 
<h3 id="module-federation-runtime">Module Federation runtime<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#module-federation-runtime"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<p>The host bootstraps Module Federation and exposes a single loader.</p>
<pre class="astro-code tokyo-night" style="background-color:#1a1b26;color:#a9b1d6;overflow-x:auto;white-space:pre-wrap;word-wrap:break-word" tabindex="0" data-language="ts"><code><span class="line"><span style="color:#51597D;font-style:italic">// apps/host/src/mf.ts</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#7DCFFF">import</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> {</span></span>

<span class="line"><span style="color:#C0CAF5">window</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">.</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7">getComponent</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> =</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> (</span><span style="color:#E0AF68">id</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">:</span><span style="color:#0DB9D7"> string</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">)</span><span style="color:#BB9AF7"> =&gt;</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> {</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#BB9AF7;font-style:italic">  return</span><span style="color:#9D7CD8;font-style:italic"> async</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> () </span><span style="color:#BB9AF7">=&gt;</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> {</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#9D7CD8;font-style:italic">    const</span><span style="color:#BB9AF7"> mod</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> =</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> (</span><span style="color:#BB9AF7;font-style:italic">await</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7"> loadRemote</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">(</span><span style="color:#C0CAF5">id</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">)) </span><span style="color:#89DDFF">as</span><span style="color:#0DB9D7"> any</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#BB9AF7;font-style:italic">    return</span><span style="color:#C0CAF5"> mod</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">.</span><span style="color:#7DCFFF">default</span><span style="color:#BB9AF7"> ||</span><span style="color:#C0CAF5"> mod</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#9ABDF5">  }</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#9ABDF5">}</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span></code><button type="button" class="copy" data-code="// apps/host/src/mf.ts
import {
  createInstance,
  loadRemote,
} from &#34;@module-federation/enhanced/runtime&#34;;

declare global {
  interface Window {
    getComponent: (id: string) => () => Promise<any>;
  }
}

createInstance({
  name: &#34;host&#34;,
  remotes: [
    {
      name: &#34;decide&#34;,
      entry: &#34;http://localhost:5175/mf-manifest.json&#34;,
      alias: &#34;decide&#34;,
    },
    {
      name: &#34;explore&#34;,
      entry: &#34;http://localhost:3004/mf-manifest.json&#34;,
      alias: &#34;explore&#34;,
    },
    {
      name: &#34;checkout&#34;,
      entry: &#34;http://localhost:3003/mf-manifest.json&#34;,
      alias: &#34;checkout&#34;,
    },
  ],
  plugins: [
    {
      name: &#34;fallback-plugin&#34;,
      errorLoadRemote(args: any) {
        console.warn(`Failed to load remote: ${args.id}`, args.error);
        return {
          default: {
            template: `<div style=&#34;padding: 2rem; text-align: center; border: 1px solid #ddd; border-radius: 8px; background: #f9f9f9; margin: 1rem 0;&#34;>
              <h3 style=&#34;color: #c00; margin-bottom: 1rem;&#34;>Remote unavailable</h3>
              <p><strong>Remote:</strong> ${args.id}</p>
              <p>Try again or check the service.</p>
            </div>`,
          },
        };
      },
    },
  ],
});

window.getComponent = (id: string) => {
  return async () => {
    const mod = (await loadRemote(id)) as any;
    return mod.default || mod;
  };
};" onclick="
            navigator.clipboard.writeText(this.dataset.code);
            this.classList.add('copied');
            setTimeout(() => this.classList.remove('copied'), 3000);
          " aria-label="Copy code"><span class="ready"></span><span class="success"></span></button></pre>
<p><strong>Why this setup</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The host is the single source of truth for remote URLs and versions.</li>
<li>URLs can change without rebuilding remotes.</li>
<li>The fallback plugin gives a consistent error experience.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="communication">Communication<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#communication"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<p>We avoid a shared global store. We use two small patterns that keep coupling low.</p>
<div class="alert alert-important astro-7kdbuayl"> <p class="alert-title astro-7kdbuayl"> <span class="alert-icon astro-7kdbuayl">📢</span> Why we do not need Pinia </p> <div class="alert-content astro-7kdbuayl"> <p>A global store looks handy. In microfrontends it creates tight runtime coupling. That kills independent deploys.</p><p>What goes wrong:</p><ul>
<li>Lockstep releases (one store change breaks other teams)</li>
<li>Hidden contracts (store shape is an API that drifts)</li>
<li>Boot order traps (who creates the store and plugins)</li>
<li>Bigger blast radius (a store error can break the whole app)</li>
<li>Harder tests (cross team mocks and brittle fixtures)</li>
</ul><p>Do this instead:</p><ul>
<li>Each microfrontend owns its state</li>
<li>Communicate with explicit custom events</li>
<li>Use URL and localStorage for simple shared reads</li>
<li>Share code not state (tokens, UI, pure utils)</li>
<li>If shared state grows, revisit boundaries rather than centralize it</li>
</ul> </div> </div> 
<div class="alert alert-info astro-7kdbuayl"> <p class="alert-title astro-7kdbuayl"> <span class="alert-icon astro-7kdbuayl"></span> 💡 Alternative: VueUse EventBus </p> <div class="alert-content astro-7kdbuayl"> <p>You could use VueUse’s <code>useEventBus</code> for more Vue-like event communication
instead of vanilla JavaScript events. It provides a cleaner API with
TypeScript support and automatic cleanup in component lifecycle. However,
adding VueUse means another dependency in your microfrontends. The tradeoff is
developer experience vs. bundle size and dependency management: vanilla
JavaScript events keep things lightweight and framework-agnostic.</p> </div> </div> 
<h3 id="navigation-through-custom-events">Navigation through custom events<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#navigation-through-custom-events"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<p>Remotes dispatch <code>mf:navigate</code> with <code>{ to }</code>. The host listens and calls <code>router.push</code>.</p>
<pre class="astro-code tokyo-night" style="background-color:#1a1b26;color:#a9b1d6;overflow-x:auto;white-space:pre-wrap;word-wrap:break-word" tabindex="0" data-language="ts"><code><span class="line"><span style="color:#51597D;font-style:italic">// apps/host/src/main.ts</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#C0CAF5">window</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">.</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7">addEventListener</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">(</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#9ECE6A">mf:navigate</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">,</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> (</span><span style="color:#E0AF68">e</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">:</span><span style="color:#C0CAF5"> Event</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">)</span><span style="color:#BB9AF7"> =&gt;</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> {</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#9D7CD8;font-style:italic">  const</span><span style="color:#BB9AF7"> to</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> =</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> (</span><span style="color:#C0CAF5">e</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> as</span><span style="color:#C0CAF5"> CustomEvent</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">)</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">.</span><span style="color:#C0CAF5">detail</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">?.</span><span style="color:#7DCFFF">to</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#BB9AF7">  if</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> (</span><span style="color:#C0CAF5">to</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">) </span><span style="color:#C0CAF5">router</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">.</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7">push</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">(</span><span style="color:#C0CAF5">to</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">)</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#9ABDF5">})</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span></code><button type="button" class="copy" data-code="// apps/host/src/main.ts
window.addEventListener(&#34;mf:navigate&#34;, (e: Event) => {
  const to = (e as CustomEvent).detail?.to;
  if (to) router.push(to);
});" onclick="

<h3 id="cart-sync-through-localstorage-plus-events">Cart sync through localStorage plus events<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#cart-sync-through-localstorage-plus-events"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<p>The checkout microfrontend owns cart logic. It listens for <code>add-to-cart</code> and <code>remove-from-cart</code>. After each change, it writes to localStorage and dispatches <code>updated-cart</code>. Any component can listen and re read.</p>
<pre class="astro-code tokyo-night" style="background-color:#1a1b26;color:#a9b1d6;overflow-x:auto;white-space:pre-wrap;word-wrap:break-word" tabindex="0" data-language="ts"><code><span class="line"><span style="color:#51597D;font-style:italic">// apps/checkout/src/stores/cartStore.ts</span></span>

<span class="line"><span style="color:#9D7CD8;font-style:italic">  const</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> {</span><span style="color:#BB9AF7"> sku</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> }</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> =</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> (</span><span style="color:#C0CAF5">ev</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> as</span><span style="color:#C0CAF5"> CustomEvent</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">)</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">.</span><span style="color:#7DCFFF">detail</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#51597D;font-style:italic">  // update cart array here</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#C0CAF5">  localStorage</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">.</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7">setItem</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">(</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#9ECE6A">cart</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">,</span><span style="color:#0DB9D7"> JSON</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">.</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7">stringify</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">(</span><span style="color:#C0CAF5">cart</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">))</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#C0CAF5">  window</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">.</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7">dispatchEvent</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">(</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">new</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7"> CustomEvent</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">(</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#9ECE6A">updated-cart</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">))</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#9ABDF5">})</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span></code><button type="button" class="copy" data-code="// apps/checkout/src/stores/cartStore.ts

  localStorage.setItem(&#34;cart&#34;, JSON.stringify(cart));

<h2 id="styling">Styling<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#styling"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<ul>
<li>Design tokens in <code>packages/shared</code> (CSS variables).</li>
<li>Shared UI in <code>packages/shared/ui</code> (Button, Input, Card).</li>
<li>Local isolation with Vue scoped styles or BEM with team prefixes (<code>e_</code>, <code>d_</code>, <code>c_</code>, <code>h_</code>).</li>
<li>Host provides <code>.mf-loading</code> and <code>.mf-error</code> classes for fallback UI.</li>
</ul>
<p>Example with BEM plus team prefix:</p>

<span class="line"><span style="color:#7AA2F7">  color</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">:</span><span style="color:#0DB9D7"> var</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">(</span><span style="color:#C0CAF5">--color-primary</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">)</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>

<p>Or Vue scoped styles:</p>
<pre class="astro-code tokyo-night" style="background-color:#1a1b26;color:#a9b1d6;overflow-x:auto;white-space:pre-wrap;word-wrap:break-word" tabindex="0" data-language="vue"><code><span class="line"><span style="color:#BA3C97">&lt;</span><span style="color:#F7768E">template</span><span style="color:#BA3C97">&gt;</span></span>

<h2 id="operations">Operations<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#operations"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<p>Plan for failure and keep the shell alive.</p>
<ul>
<li>Each remote shows a clear loading state and a clear error state.</li>
<li>Navigation works even if a remote fails.</li>
<li>Logs are visible in the host during development.</li>
</ul>
<p>Global styles in the host help here:</p>
<pre class="astro-code tokyo-night" style="background-color:#1a1b26;color:#a9b1d6;overflow-x:auto;white-space:pre-wrap;word-wrap:break-word" tabindex="0" data-language="css"><code><span class="line"><span style="color:#51597D;font-style:italic">/* apps/host/src/styles.css */</span></span>

<h2 id="more-module-federation-features-short-hints">More Module Federation features (short hints)<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#more-module-federation-features-short-hints"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<p>Our solution is simple on purpose. Module Federation can do more. Use these when your app needs them.</p>
<p><strong>Prefetch</strong> (requires registering lazyLoadComponentPlugin)<br/>
Pre load JS, CSS, and data for a remote before the user clicks (for example on hover). This cuts wait time.</p>
<pre class="astro-code tokyo-night" style="background-color:#1a1b26;color:#a9b1d6;overflow-x:auto;white-space:pre-wrap;word-wrap:break-word" tabindex="0" data-language="js"><code><span class="line"><span style="color:#51597D;font-style:italic">// after registering lazyLoadComponentPlugin on the runtime instance</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#7DCFFF">import</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> { </span><span style="color:#0DB9D7">getInstance</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> }</span><span style="color:#7DCFFF"> from</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> &quot;</span><span style="color:#9ECE6A">@module-federation/enhanced/runtime</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>
<span class="line"></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#9D7CD8;font-style:italic">const</span><span style="color:#BB9AF7"> mf</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> =</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7"> getInstance</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">()</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#BB9AF7">function</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7"> onHover</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">()</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> {</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#C0CAF5">  mf</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">.</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7">prefetch</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">({</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#73DACA">    id</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">:</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> &quot;</span><span style="color:#9ECE6A">shop/Button</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">,</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#73DACA">    dataFetchParams</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">:</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> { </span><span style="color:#73DACA">productId</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">:</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> &quot;</span><span style="color:#9ECE6A">12345</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> }</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">,</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#73DACA">    preloadComponentResource</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">:</span><span style="color:#FF9E64"> true</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">,</span><span style="color:#51597D;font-style:italic"> // also fetch JS and CSS</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#9ABDF5">  })</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#9ABDF5">}</span></span></code><button type="button" class="copy" data-code="// after registering lazyLoadComponentPlugin on the runtime instance
import { getInstance } from &#34;@module-federation/enhanced/runtime&#34;;

const mf = getInstance();
function onHover() {
  mf.prefetch({
    id: &#34;shop/Button&#34;,
    dataFetchParams: { productId: &#34;12345&#34; },
    preloadComponentResource: true, // also fetch JS and CSS
  });
}" onclick="
            navigator.clipboard.writeText(this.dataset.code);
            this.classList.add('copied');
            setTimeout(() => this.classList.remove('copied'), 3000);
          " aria-label="Copy code"><span class="ready"></span><span class="success"></span></button></pre>
<p><strong>Component level data fetching</strong><br/>
Expose a <code>.data</code> loader next to a component. The consumer can ask the runtime to fetch data before render (works in CSR and SSR). Use a <code>.data.client.ts</code> file for client loaders when SSR falls back.</p>
<p><strong>Caching for loaders</strong><br/>
Wrap expensive loaders in a cache helper (with maxAge, revalidate, tag, and custom keys). You get stale while revalidate behavior and tag based invalidation.</p>
<pre class="astro-code tokyo-night" style="background-color:#1a1b26;color:#a9b1d6;overflow-x:auto;white-space:pre-wrap;word-wrap:break-word" tabindex="0" data-language="js"><code><span class="line"><span style="color:#51597D;font-style:italic">// inside your DataLoader file</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#9D7CD8;font-style:italic">const</span><span style="color:#BB9AF7"> fetchDashboard</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> =</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7"> cache</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">(</span><span style="color:#9D7CD8;font-style:italic">async</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> ()</span><span style="color:#BB9AF7"> =&gt;</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7"> getStats</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">()</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">,</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> {</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#73DACA">  maxAge</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">:</span><span style="color:#FF9E64"> 120000</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">,</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#73DACA">  revalidate</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">:</span><span style="color:#FF9E64"> 60000</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">,</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#9ABDF5">})</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span></code><button type="button" class="copy" data-code="// inside your DataLoader file
const fetchDashboard = cache(async () => getStats(), {
  maxAge: 120000,
  revalidate: 60000,
});" onclick="
            navigator.clipboard.writeText(this.dataset.code);
            this.classList.add('copied');
            setTimeout(() => this.classList.remove('copied'), 3000);
          " aria-label="Copy code"><span class="ready"></span><span class="success"></span></button></pre>
<p><strong>Type hinting for remotes</strong><br/>
<code>@module-federation/enhanced</code> can generate types for exposes. Add this to tsconfig.json so editors resolve remote types and hot reload them.</p>
<pre class="astro-code tokyo-night" style="background-color:#1a1b26;color:#a9b1d6;overflow-x:auto;white-space:pre-wrap;word-wrap:break-word" tabindex="0" data-language="json"><code><span class="line"><span style="color:#9ABDF5">{</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#89DDFF">  &quot;</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7">compilerOptions</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">:</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> {</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> &quot;</span><span style="color:#0DB9D7">paths</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">:</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> {</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> &quot;</span><span style="color:#7DCFFF">*</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">:</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> [</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#9ECE6A">./@mf-types/*</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">]</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> }</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> }</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">,</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#89DDFF">  &quot;</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7">include</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">:</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> [</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#9ECE6A">./@mf-types/*</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">]</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#9ABDF5">}</span></span></code><button type="button" class="copy" data-code="{
  &#34;compilerOptions&#34;: { &#34;paths&#34;: { &#34;*&#34;: [&#34;./@mf-types/*&#34;] } },
  &#34;include&#34;: [&#34;./@mf-types/*&#34;]
}" onclick="
            navigator.clipboard.writeText(this.dataset.code);
            this.classList.add('copied');
            setTimeout(() => this.classList.remove('copied'), 3000);
          " aria-label="Copy code"><span class="ready"></span><span class="success"></span></button></pre>
<p><strong>Vue bridge for app level modules</strong><br/>
Mount a whole remote Vue app into a route when you need an application level integration (not just a component).</p>
<pre class="astro-code tokyo-night" style="background-color:#1a1b26;color:#a9b1d6;overflow-x:auto;white-space:pre-wrap;word-wrap:break-word" tabindex="0" data-language="js"><code><span class="line"><span style="color:#7DCFFF">import</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> { </span><span style="color:#0DB9D7">createRemoteAppComponent</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> }</span><span style="color:#7DCFFF"> from</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> &quot;</span><span style="color:#9ECE6A">@module-federation/bridge-vue3</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#9D7CD8;font-style:italic">const</span><span style="color:#BB9AF7"> RemoteApp</span><span style="color:#89DDFF"> =</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7"> createRemoteAppComponent</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">({</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#7AA2F7">  loader</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">:</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5"> ()</span><span style="color:#BB9AF7"> =&gt;</span><span style="color:#7AA2F7"> loadRemote</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">(</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#9ECE6A">remote1/export-app</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">&quot;</span><span style="color:#9ABDF5">)</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">,</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#9ABDF5">})</span><span style="color:#89DDFF">;</span></span>
<span class="line"><span style="color:#51597D;font-style:italic">// router: { path: &#39;/remote1/:pathMatch(.*)*&#39;, component: RemoteApp }</span></span></code><button type="button" class="copy" data-code="import { createRemoteAppComponent } from &#34;@module-federation/bridge-vue3&#34;;
const RemoteApp = createRemoteAppComponent({
  loader: () => loadRemote(&#34;remote1/export-app&#34;),
});
// router: { path: '/remote1/:pathMatch(.*)*', component: RemoteApp }" onclick="
            navigator.clipboard.writeText(this.dataset.code);
            this.classList.add('copied');
            setTimeout(() => this.classList.remove('copied'), 3000);
          " aria-label="Copy code"><span class="ready"></span><span class="success"></span></button></pre>
<p>You can read more about these interesting techniques at <a href="https://module-federation.io/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">module-federation.io</a>.</p>
<h3 id="summary">Summary<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#summary"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<p>This was my first attempt to understand <strong>microfrontends</strong> better while solving the <em>Tractor Store</em> exercise.</p>
<p>In the future, I may also try it with <strong>SSR</strong> and <strong>universal rendering</strong>, which I find interesting.</p>

      function initInternalLinks() {
        const wrappers = document.querySelectorAll(".internal-link-wrapper");

        wrappers.forEach(wrapper => {
          const card = wrapper.querySelector(".preview-card");
          const link = wrapper.querySelector(".internal-link");
          if (!card || !link) return;

          // Skip if already initialized
          if (wrapper.dataset.initialized === "true") return;
          wrapper.dataset.initialized = "true";

          // Function to hide the card
          const hideCard = () => {
            card.classList.remove("is-fixed");
            card.style.removeProperty("--pc-top");
            card.style.removeProperty("--pc-left");
            card.style.opacity = "";
            card.style.visibility = "";
            // Remove scroll listener when hiding
            window.removeEventListener("scroll", hideCard);
          };

          wrapper.addEventListener("mouseenter", () => {
            // Make visible first so it has size
            card.style.opacity = "1";
            card.style.visibility = "visible";

            // Use fixed positioning to escape overflow clipping
            const linkRect = link.getBoundingClientRect();
            const cardRect = card.getBoundingClientRect();

            // Position above by default; flip below if too close to top
            const aboveTop = linkRect.top - 8 - cardRect.height;
            const belowTop = linkRect.bottom + 8;
            const top = aboveTop < 10 ? belowTop : aboveTop;

            // Center horizontally on the link
            const left = linkRect.left + linkRect.width / 2 - cardRect.width / 2;

            // Constrain to viewport
            const vw = document.documentElement.clientWidth;
            const safeLeft = Math.max(8, Math.min(left, vw - cardRect.width - 8));

            // Apply fixed position with coordinates
            card.classList.add("is-fixed");
            card.style.setProperty("--pc-top", `${Math.round(top)}px`);
            card.style.setProperty("--pc-left", `${Math.round(safeLeft)}px`);

            // Hide card on scroll
            window.addEventListener("scroll", hideCard, { passive: true });
          });

          wrapper.addEventListener("mouseleave", hideCard);
        });
      }

      // Initialize on both initial load and after client-side navigation
      document.addEventListener("astro:page-load", initInternalLinks);
    </script> </body> </html>  <script>(function(){const postSlug = "how-to-build-microfrontends-with-module-federation-and-vue";

  function updateCTAFollowVisibility() {
    const cta = document.getElementById("cta-follow");
    const article = document.getElementById("article");
    if (!cta || !article) return;

    // If it has the force-hidden class, don't try to show it
    if (cta.classList.contains("force-hidden")) {
      return;
    }

    const viewportHeight = window.innerHeight;
    const articleBottom = article.getBoundingClientRect().bottom;

    // Only show if user has reached the end of the article (article bottom is visible)
    // and hasn't dismissed or subscribed
    if (
      articleBottom <= viewportHeight + 100 && // 100px buffer
      !localStorage.getItem("newsletter_dismissed") &&
      !localStorage.getItem("newsletter_subscribed")
    ) {
      cta.dataset.visible = "true";
      cta.style.transform = "translateX(0)";
      cta.style.opacity = "1";
    } else {
      cta.dataset.visible = "false";
      cta.style.transform = "translateX(-120%)";
      cta.style.opacity = "0";
    }
  }

  // Initialize visibility check
  window.addEventListener("scroll", updateCTAFollowVisibility);
  window.addEventListener("resize", updateCTAFollowVisibility);

  // Add a small delay to initial check to ensure proper positioning
  setTimeout(updateCTAFollowVisibility, 500);

  // Handle newsletter subscribe click with proper tracking
  document
    .getElementById("newsletter-subscribe-button")
    ?.addEventListener("click", () => {
      localStorage.setItem("newsletter_subscribed", "true");

      // Force the popup to stay hidden
      const cta = document.getElementById("cta-follow");
      if (cta) {
        cta.classList.add("force-hidden");
        cta.style.transform = "translateX(-120%)";
        cta.style.opacity = "0";
      }

      if (window.plausible) {
        window.plausible("Newsletter Subscribe Click", {
          props: {
            post: postSlug,
            location: "end_of_article",
            source: "notification",
          },
        });
      }
    });

  // Handle newsletter dismiss click
  document
    .getElementById("newsletter-dismiss")
    ?.addEventListener("click", function () {
      const slug = this.getAttribute("data-post-slug");
      localStorage.setItem("newsletter_dismissed", "true");

      const cta = document.getElementById("cta-follow");
      if (cta) {
        cta.classList.add("force-hidden");
        cta.style.transform = "translateX(-120%)";
        cta.style.opacity = "0";
      }

      if (window.plausible) {
        window.plausible("Newsletter Dismissed", {
          props: {
            post: slug,
            location: "end_of_article",
            source: "notification",
          },
        });
      }
    });
})();</script>  <script>
  /** Create a progress indicator
   *  at the top */
  function createProgressBar() {
    // Create the main container div
    const progressContainer = document.createElement("div");
    progressContainer.className =
      "progress-container fixed top-0 z-10 h-1 w-full bg-skin-fill";

    // Create the progress bar div
    const progressBar = document.createElement("div");
    progressBar.className = "progress-bar h-1 w-0 bg-skin-accent";
    progressBar.id = "myBar";

    // Append the progress bar to the progress container
    progressContainer.appendChild(progressBar);

    // Append the progress container to the document body or any other desired parent element
    document.body.appendChild(progressContainer);
  }
  createProgressBar();

  /** Update the progress bar
   *  when user scrolls */
  function updateScrollProgress() {
    const winScroll =
      document.body.scrollTop || document.documentElement.scrollTop;
    const height =
      document.documentElement.scrollHeight -
      document.documentElement.clientHeight;
    const scrolled = (winScroll / height) * 100;
    const myBar = document.getElementById("myBar");
    if (myBar) {
      myBar.style.width = scrolled + "%";
    }
  }
  document.addEventListener("scroll", updateScrollProgress);

  /** Make headings groups for hover effect on anchor links */
  function makeHeadingsGroups() {
    const headings = Array.from(
      document.querySelectorAll(".prose h2, .prose h3, .prose h4, .prose h5, .prose h6")
    );
    for (const heading of headings) {
      heading.classList.add("group");
    }
  }

  // Run after DOM is loaded
  if (document.readyState === "loading") {
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", makeHeadingsGroups);
  } else {
    makeHeadingsGroups();
  }

  /** Scroll back to top functionality */
  function attachBackToTop() {
    const backToTopBtn = document.getElementById("back-to-top");
    if (backToTopBtn) {
      backToTopBtn.addEventListener("click", () => {
        window.scrollTo({ top: 0, behavior: "smooth" });
      });
    }
  }
  attachBackToTop();
</script>
